  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8fb87d9a-e98b-474d-806d-032d31f0ee4d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8236063130742465479">What would you do to save someone you love?<br/><br/>Time is slipping away. . . .<br/><br/>Tella Holloway is losing it.   <span id="freeText8236063130742465479" style="display:none">What would you do to save someone you love?<br /><br />Time is slipping away. . . .<br /><br />Tella Holloway is losing it. Her brother is sick, and when a dozen doctors can't determine what's wrong, her parents decide to move to the middle of nowhere for the fresh air. She's lost her friends, her parents are driving her crazy, her brother is dying--and she's helpless to change anything.<br /><br />Until she receives mysterious instructions on how to become a Contender in the Brimstone Bleed. It's an epic race across jungle, desert, ocean, and mountain that could win her the prize she desperately desires: the Cure for her brother's illness. But all the Contenders are after the Cure for people they love, and there's no guarantee that Tella (or any of them) will survive the race.<br /><br />The jungle is terrifying, the clock is ticking, and Tella knows she can't trust the allies she makes. And one big question emerges: Why have so many fallen sick in the first place?<br /><br />Victoria Scott's breathtaking novel grabs readers by the throat and doesn't let go.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=jericho-fucking-barrons">jericho-fucking-barrons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=quest">quest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer688936676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11833832727540273552"><blockquote>
  <i>The woman pauses dramatically. “I’d like to officially welcome you to the Brimstone Bleed. May the bravest Contender win.”</i>
</blockquote>Wait, what?<blockquote>
  <i>“Put this on your shirt.”<br/>It’s a small gold serpent pin, and it’s fairly heavy.</i>
</blockquote><b>Well, isn't that just fucking special?</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392878880ra/8626999.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This book is half <i>Hunger Games</i>, half Digimon/Pokémon hybrid, and 100% terrible.</b> The writing and the main character is absolutely juvenile---without all the sexual scenes, this book would feel like it was written for a middle grade audience bec</span>
  <span id="freeText11833832727540273552" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>The woman pauses dramatically. “I’d like to officially welcome you to the Brimstone Bleed. May the bravest Contender win.”</i>
</blockquote>Wait, what?<blockquote>
  <i>“Put this on your shirt.”<br>It’s a small gold serpent pin, and it’s fairly heavy.</i>
</blockquote><b>Well, isn't that just fucking special?</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392878880ra/8626999.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This book is half <i>Hunger Games</i>, half Digimon/Pokémon hybrid, and 100% terrible.</b> The writing and the main character is absolutely juvenile---without all the sexual scenes, this book would feel like it was written for a middle grade audience because of the utter immaturity (and imbecility) of its main character.<br><br>Let's get the obvious over with: this is a <i>Hunger Games</i> wannabe, without the setting, without the complexity of the characters, without the depth. I wouldn't call this a clone, because for one thing...this book doesn't work. At all. Comparing this book to <i>The Hunger Games</i> would be a gross insult to the original books.<br><br>You see, this book takes place in a contemporary setting. We start in Montana, the United States. Quickly, we are plunged into rainforests, jungles, deserts. Nothing makes any sense.<br><br><u>The Summary</u>:<br><br><b>I: OOH! MYSTERIOUS DEVICE! MUST OBEY!</b><br><br>16-year old Tella is a fucking moron. Her older brother, Cody, is sick. He is wasting away, and her family has decided to uproot themselves to Montana so he can get all the fresh air and stuff in an effort to cure him. Like people with consumption in the 19th century move to the West so they can get away from all the bad humors in the city.<br><br>There's just one problem: it's 2014, and it's Montana.<br><br>Tella is, like a typical 16-year old, really not into the move. She wants Facebook. She wants technology. She will die without her phone. One night, she goes into her room...only to find a mysterious blue-wrapped box on her bed. A BOX!!!!<blockquote>
  <i>Holding the box to my lips, I tell it, “You’re mine, precious. All mine.”</i>
</blockquote>The box holds a device the size of a hearing aid with a blinking red button. Tella pushes it, this message plays:<blockquote>
  <i>“If you’re hearing this message, you are invited to be a Contender in the Brimstone Bleed. All Contenders must report within forty-eight hours to select their Pandora companions.”</i>
</blockquote>Tella doesn't fucking know who left her the message. She doesn't know how the box got there. Her parents are trying to hide the box from her, to the extent of literally setting the box on fire.<br><br>Tella digs it out of the flames anyway. The message continues. It promises her something great.<blockquote>
  <i>“The Brimstone Bleed will last three months and will take place across four ecosystems: desert, sea, mountains, jungle. The winning prize will be the Cure — a remedy for any illness, for any single person.”</i>
</blockquote>Well, howdy doody! She doesn't know who fucking left the message, or how the person is going to cure her brother when modern science already says that there is no cure for her brother, but fuck, let's do it! <b>Let's just listen to the mysterious message from god-knows-who, let's just run off in the middle of the fucking night to god-knows-where, only to disappear from your parents for 3 fucking months (nobody cares about missing children, anyway, right?), in order to pursue a mysterious cure for your brother in a race involving god-knows-what!</b><br><br>Makes perfect sense to me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392878880ra/8627000.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So good old Tella defies her parents, steals their car---she takes the crappy car, of course, being the amazing daughter she is: <blockquote>
  <i>And after almost two hundred thousand miles, the car is an utter embarrassment to the auto community. My parents will wake up to find their daughter gone. I’d hate to have them left with the crap car, too.</i>
</blockquote>SUCH FILIAL PIETY.<br><br><b>II: EGGS, SEXY SERIAL KILLERS, AND A MYSTERIOUS PILL</b><br><br>So Tella runs away, to an empty museum in the middle of nowhere, like the message told her. <b>In any other book, you could almost guarantee that the heroine who does this shit would end up the victim of a serial killer.</b> An empty museum, in the dead of night in the middle of nowhere.<br><br><b>Tella's instincts are telling her RUN RUN RUN. Fuck instincts, what are they good for, anyway?</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’ve watched a lot of scary movies, and I’ve learned nothing good is ever at the bottom of a winding staircase. Pulling in a breath and preparing myself to be eaten alive, I head down.</i>
</blockquote>In the middle of a room are an assortment of eggs. Large eggs, small eggs. Shiny ones, iridescent ones.<br><br><b>If I wandered into a room full of eggs, my first thought would be "Where's the fucking bacon? I want to make an omelet!!" But not brilliant Tella; she just knows the eggs are there for a purpose.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I don’t need the device in my pocket to tell me what my gut already knows.<br>This is the Pandora Selection Process.</i>
</blockquote>While Tella is standing there, wondering about the meaning of life, a million other contestants rush in and grab all the eggs (fucking brilliant). Tella manages, by the skin of her teeth, to snatch the very last one.<br><br>She is then introduced to our love interest #1: the sexy serial killer.<blockquote>
  <i>He looks back at me, and I wonder if maybe, even though he looks a little like a serial killer, he’s going to help me up.</i>
</blockquote>They go to a train station, where they are met by an Effie-Trinket school reject in garish, loud clothes, and handed a pill. Naturally, MUST TAKE THE PILL.<br><br><b>III: THE JUNGLE! THE DESERT! THE...EGGS?</b><br><br>Regret is the morning after. Tella wakes up.<blockquote>
  <i>Pounding my fists against the boards, I scream. I swallowed the pill. I’m in a box. How stupid could I have been? I left without telling my family where I was going, got on a train to a city that doesn’t exist, and swallowed a foreign object. Oh yeah, and I also picked up a rotting egg along the way.</i>
</blockquote>This type of self-realization is important; in my native language, we have a phrase for it that roughly translates to <i>"you are so fucking dumb that when you die and join us in the land of the dead, we will pretend that you don't exist because you are an embarrassment to our family line."</i><br><br>Just kidding.<br><br>Tella wakes up in a motherfucking jungle. It is a race, and the first legs are through the jungle and the desert. It's not a race to the death, because there are 4 legs of the race along the way. The competitors can join forces, and it's damned good thing they do, because Tella is so fucking helpless she wouldn't survive without their help.<br><br>Along the way, the eggs hatch. They hatch into a fox, an elephant, a raccoon, a bear, an eagle.<br><br>Tella punches that eagle. A BALD EAGLE. <b>She just sucker punched the national bird of the United States.</b><blockquote>
  <i>...when the eagle gets close enough — I swing a right hook and collide with the bird. She slams into the ground and slides for several feet.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392878880ra/8627001.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It turns out this is a race. <b>This is more <i>The Amazing Race</i> (the TV show), than anything resembling <i>The Hunger Games</i>.</b><br><br><u>The Premise</u>: Fucking ludicrous. I don't know why the fuck this book is shelved under "dystopia," it is not. It is modern-day United States, and the premise of a Hunger Games race is simply idiotic. I don't know why the fuck all these people are there. I don't know why the fuck <b>there are child contestants---some barely 10</b>. I don't know why the Big Bad Guys (and there are always Big Bad Guys) are doing this in the first place, when they supposedly have a cure for all kinds of illnesses.<br><br>The people who run this race are called Pharmies, as in Pharmaceuticals. I don't know if you guys know this, but pharmaceuticals and the drug industries are worth hundreds of billions of dollars. <b>If these guys have the cure to every fucking thing, why are they just limiting this to a stupid pointless race when they could be making major bucks for their discovery?</b> It makes no fucking sense.<br><br>Why the fuck are we in the desert? Where the fuck is this motherfucking jungle? Did anyone question this shit? No. Is it in Africa? Maybe. It could only be Africa, considering the fact that the contestants get attacked by fucking gorillas.<br><br>Does the people running this competition wonder, well, MAYBE PEOPLE ARE GOING TO QUESTION THE FACT THAT THEIR LOVED ONES ARE DISAPPEARING FOR MONTHS AT A TIME. No. Some of these kids are well, KIDS. You think maybe someone's going to wonder OH THEY'RE MISSING SCHOOL FOR 3 MONTHS, YOU THINK?<br><br><u>DIGIMON, DIGITAL MONSTERS, DIGIMONS ARE THE CHAMPIONS!</u> Oh, the eggs. <b>They're fucking Digimon eggs, guys.</b> Seriously, these people are given fucking eggs that hatch into creatures.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392878880i/8627002.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, not exactly like that, they're normal creatures, like eagles, raccoons...<br><br>Elephants.<br><br>WHAT'S THE FUCKING POINT OF HATCHING SHIT IN EGGS? IS A NORMAL WOMB NOT SUFFICIENT?<br><br>These creatures are actually rather special, they have special abilities. Like Digimons, they...morph.<blockquote>
  <i>His head falls back and his spine ripples. Beneath him, his legs and arms stretch longer and wider, and his black coat begins to thicken. My Pandora grows massive muscles and new body parts — morphing.</i>
</blockquote>Not ondo they morph, they <b>duel each other in a Pokémon style duel to the death. They Digivolve.</b> Cute.<br><br><u>TELLA-HER TO SHUT UP</u>: <b>Tella is the most annoyingly grating heroine I've read in a long time. The narration is first-person, and it is simply intolerable.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I close my hand around the lid and pull it off. Inside is a tiny pillow. I imagine all sorts of miniature animals using it in their miniature beds. But that’s dumb, because how would they ever find a pillow case to fit?</i>
</blockquote>Tella is so juvenile, so immature. She has the dumbest trains of thoughts. Every time she goes into a long-winded narration, I wanted to punch her in the face. She talks to herself. CONSTANTLY. UNCEASINGLY. WILL IT EVER STOP?<blockquote>
  <i>I decide to stay put but reason that if I see another Contender soon, I’ll run my tag-team idea across them. Deal? Deal.<br><br>Oh Jesus. I’m already talking to myself. Or thinking to myself as if there are two of me. Is that the same thing? I’m not sure. But I do know I’ve been alone for two minutes and I’m already losing my shit.</i>
</blockquote>NO, IT DOESN'T.<br><br><u>TELLA-HER THAT LOOKS AREN'T EVERYTHING</u>:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392879245ra/8627045.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Tella is a fucking moron, I've said it before, and I really mean it.</b> She makes the dumbest fucking decisions. <b>While deciding what to pack for the competition, instead of, like...survival shit, emergency food, warm clothes, matches...she thinks...OOH, I NEED NAIL POLISH.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Because I have no idea of what I’ll need, I also throw in random things from my desk: pens, paper, scissors, tape. The last thing I pack is a photo of my family that’s stuck in the edge of my mirror. That and my glittery purple nail polish.</i>
</blockquote>Tella is hurt, bleeding, she needs to get her ass on in the competition so that she doesn't fall behind the other contestants. What does she do first? WHY, FIX HER FACE.<blockquote>
  <i>Running my fingers through my hair, I think about how I should be racing toward Lincoln Station. But the compulsion to repair my face is too strong.<br><br>I grab my makeup bag — the one I never leave home without — and fix what I can.</i>
</blockquote>Tella is hopelessly out of shape. She's not ready for any sort of a competition. BUT SURELY, IF SHE LOOKS THE PART, SHE'LL DO JUST FUCKING FINE.<blockquote>
  <i>With curls trimmed close to my head and a roguish green-and-blue feather dangling over my right shoulder, I decide I just might seem like someone who would enter a daring race — and win.</i>
</blockquote>...<b>That's not exactly how it works.</b> During the competition, conditions are terrible. They're hungry, they lack water...Tella lacks makeup.<blockquote>
  <i>For a fleeting moment, before the woman speaks, I pray that the orange pack I’m wearing holds Chanel makeup. And a brush. And a mirror.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Plot</u>: All action, no sense, no excitement. There is no competition, because this is a survival race as they go through each terrain. <b>I was never engrossed in the plot because there was largely no point to this book.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392878880ra/8627003.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>The Other Characters</u>: None of the characters in this book stand out. I can't remember any of them. The only character that stands out is the 8 and 10 year old kids because they are so completely young and out of place. The other characters have no personality, I cannot be fucked to remember who is Caroline, who is Harper, who is Ransom. The love interests are douchebags, both of them. One looks like a serial killer with a heart of gold, the other is a serial killer who looks like the boy next door. One is slightly less loathsome than the other.<br><br>They start off uneasily. All of a sudden, before 50% of the book is through, they're making out and they're in luuuuuuuuurve. I don't get it.<br><br>I want to point you guys to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825458283" rel="nofollow noopener">Cory's review</a> of this book, because she explains the perpetration of rape culture in this book much better than I can. This review has wasted enough of my time already.<br><br>Needless to say, fuck this book.<br><br><i>Quotes were taken from an uncorrected proof, subject to change in the final edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11833832727540273552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_779309492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779309492" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/779309492?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779309492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13519930720469200760"><i>
  <u>There's something familiar about this story...</u>
</i><br/><br/>A group of people must compete against one another in a <b>game of survival</b>, an epic race across jungle, desert, ocean and mountain. They face the danger of their fellow competitors, as well as the various threats of nature. There can be <b>only one winner</b>.<br/><br/><i>
  <u>Where have I heard this before?</u>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392528272ra/8573731.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>During this competition, some of the competitors choose to form teams in order to increase their chances of survival out in the wilderness. There's flirtations betw</span>
  <span id="freeText13519930720469200760" style="display:none"><i>
  <u>There's something familiar about this story...</u>
</i><br><br>A group of people must compete against one another in a <b>game of survival</b>, an epic race across jungle, desert, ocean and mountain. They face the danger of their fellow competitors, as well as the various threats of nature. There can be <b>only one winner</b>.<br><br><i>
  <u>Where have I heard this before?</u>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392528272ra/8573731.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>During this competition, some of the competitors choose to form teams in order to increase their chances of survival out in the wilderness. There's flirtations between the MC and the hot, mysterious dude. And why is she doing all this again? <b>To save her brother</b>.<br><br><i>
  <u>Hang on a minute, I've definitely seen this before...</u>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392528800ra/8573815.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>'The woman pauses dramatically. "I’d like to officially welcome you to the Brimstone Bleed. <b>May the bravest Contender win</b>."'<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392528869ra/8573844.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yep. This is another book about a competition/game where there can be only one winner and the protagonist - this time called Tella Holloway - is doing it all for the sake of her sibling. There's just very little need to read this if you've already read The Hunger Games. And if you haven't read The Hunger Games, then go read that instead. Or Battle Royale. But probably not this.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069167.Fire___Flood__Fire___Flood___1_" title="Fire &amp; Flood (Fire &amp; Flood, #1) by Victoria Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire &amp; Flood</a> is more of a spectacularly average book than it is a bad one, and still might offer some entertainment to those who aren't familiar with THG or don't mind reading similar versions of the same story. I found Tella to be an uninspiring, bland main character whose narration cannot compete with either the bold, interesting Katniss or the charismatic narrator of the author's other books - Dante Walker. Ms Scott has a quirky style to her writing that can work very well at times but never really felt suited to Tella and her acute blandness. The cast of secondary characters also increases as the book moves along but none of them are particularly interesting - not even mr sexy with his impressive muscles.<br><br>Plus, I immediately started to dislike Tella after reading this:<br><br><i>The last girl I see, I want to strangle. Like the woman, she has long hair. But instead of dark, it's blond - no, honey gold - and shines like that of a Broadway starlet. I can't see her eyes from here, but I'm sure they're some kind of stunning shade of blue. She has cream-colored skin and a body that belongs in a magazine - the kind for guys, not girls. I hate her with everything I have as she laughs her perfect laugh and tosses her perfect hair and crosses her to-die-for legs... We could be friends, I realize, if I weren't so overwhelmed with the urge to end her.</i><br><br>*sigh* Will this never end in YA?<br><br>As for the positive, there was one thing I really liked. In this story, each of the competitors starts off with an egg that hatches into an animal that may or may not have special powers - these animals are called Pandoras and team up with their human companion to help them win. And Tella's Pandora is a little black fox called Madox who is more than he first seems. He likes to trot around her feet and lie on his back waving his legs in the air... <b>he is effin' adorable</b>. I swear he is the only reason this book got two stars. Let's finish with a picture of him:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392529908i/8574099.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/lm/#/users/10010/profile" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390671357i/8260477.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13519930720469200760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_894183853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/894183853" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/894183853?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who have NOTHING ELSE to read. :P</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=did-not-connect-with-characters">did-not-connect-with-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=competition">competition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer894183853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer290731211296692257"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392255ra/755181.gif' width='350' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069167.Fire___Flood__Fire___Flood___1_' title='Fire & Flood (Fire & Flood, #1) by Victoria Scott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fire & Flood</a> is a VERY disappointing read. Of course, I’ve read some reviews and saw that many said it had a lot of similarities to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>. I may be one of the few who thought that, but I didn’t mind that fact before picking it up. <i> As long as it's good and not 100% similar to that book</i>. Fortunately, it’s not <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a> all the way. <br/><br/>Tella is a normal teenager who just moved out to Montana with her family. She is loved by her parents but unfortunately, her brother is ill and she w</span>
  <span id="freeText290731211296692257" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392255ra/755181.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069167.Fire___Flood__Fire___Flood___1_" title="Fire &amp; Flood (Fire &amp; Flood, #1) by Victoria Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire &amp; Flood</a> is a VERY disappointing read. Of course, I’ve read some reviews and saw that many said it had a lot of similarities to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. I may be one of the few who thought that, but I didn’t mind that fact before picking it up. <i> As long as it's good and not 100% similar to that book</i>. Fortunately, it’s not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> all the way. <br><br>Tella is a normal teenager who just moved out to Montana with her family. She is loved by her parents but unfortunately, her brother is ill and she wants to save him desperately. When the chance of a lifetime presents itself to save her brother, she immediately takes it and decides to participate to the Brimstone Breed competition. Throughout that competition, she will meet some new friends and allies, make some enemies, fall in love and live a perilous adventure in the jungle and desert. Sounds not so bad, right? I would have thought the same thing at your place but, the thing is, this book was <i>boring.</i><br><br><i>And repetitive</i>. Before entering the competition, she has to choose an egg which contains a Pandora (animal with superpowers.) That element is quite interesting but, in fact, their superpowers are not amazing or breathtaking at all. Then, when she’s in the jungle, she decides to follow this unfriendly looking guy who looks as if he knows where he is going. <i>And she sleeps not far from him.</i> That is so careless. Tella is the kind of character that acts as if she didn’t care what people thought (in the annoying way) and does so many frustrating things that normal people would think about twice before doing them. Needless to say, I didn’t connect nor liked her. <b>She can die in the sequels, I won’t give a care. </b> <br><br>The story has potential but lacks of world-building, seriousness, depth, endearing characters, interesting challenges and purpose. Why Brimstone Breed is created is barely explained. I don’t get why there aren’t cameras following the Contenders. I mean, what’s the point of having this challenge if no one can see it? <i>Maybe because that would mean a The <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> remake?</i> Still, its purpose is basically vengeance and I think that’s a weak and mischievous one. Victoria Scott could have found a better one! <i>Right?</i><br><br>I love animals, I do. I care about the animals presented in this book. But, there were so many! I simply got tired of them. They were really the center of attention and, I don’t know, I wanted more danger, perilous challenges and also, since we’re at it, less killing each other when it isn’t even mandatory! <br><br>The writing wasn’t bad. It was actually pretty fine and the pacing mostly fast so that made the reading easier. There really aren’t many negative things I could say about it. I would have appreciated if there were fewer sentences with purpose to make something look important and poignant. It was annoying and it’s like the author wanted to make the book deep and serious but it didn’t work because the main character doesn’t have the personality for. She laughs when it isn't the time to and it just feels like they aren't veritably in danger. I didn't feel any stress or heart pounding during my reading, sadly, as I did in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>.<br><br>Overall, I think some people would like this book, but I definitely don’t recommend it to everyone. Maybe give it a try if you haven’t read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>, like competitions and like when there are (a lot of) animals in books.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="290731211296692257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_694115138" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694115138" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694115138?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=caught-in-a-bad-romance">caught-in-a-bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=losing-my-faith-in-humanity">losing-my-faith-in-humanity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=take-your-insta-love-and-leave">take-your-insta-love-and-leave</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=doesn-t-deserve-the-hype">doesn-t-deserve-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=unmet-potential">unmet-potential</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=almost-fell-asleep">almost-fell-asleep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=meh">meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694115138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14784890365595172817"><b>This is a mini-review (that actually turned out not too mini in length, but it's got the same feel as one), because this book was painfully forgettable, and other reviews have already discussed its problems in great length.</b><br/><br/>Guys, I hate to be <i>that</i> person, but this book is The Hunger Games. But then also add Digimon. And yeah, that might sound awesome, but it's really, really not. There have been <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825458283?book_show_action=false&page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>a</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688936676?book_show_action=true&page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>few</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779309492?book_show_action=false&page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>reviews</a> to point out the glaring similarities between Fire & Flood and The Hunger Games (the Eff</span>
  <span id="freeText14784890365595172817" style="display:none"><b>This is a mini-review (that actually turned out not too mini in length, but it's got the same feel as one), because this book was painfully forgettable, and other reviews have already discussed its problems in great length.</b><br /><br />Guys, I hate to be <i>that</i> person, but this book is The Hunger Games. But then also add Digimon. And yeah, that might sound awesome, but it's really, really not. There have been <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825458283?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">a</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688936676?book_show_action=true&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">few</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779309492?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">reviews</a> to point out the glaring similarities between Fire &amp; Flood and The Hunger Games (the Effie-character says, "May the bravest Contender win," for starters. And hands them a pin, you guys), so I won't, but I promise you, they're there. It's actually really baffling how this went through the processes of publishing without anyone saying, "Hey, wait..." but then again, 50 Shades is a thing, so. <br /><br />For starters, the main character is honestly one of the stupidest characters I've read about in my life. As the book starts, she gets a mysterious message saying that she has to compete in a race in order to find a cure for her brother's disease. Her parents then try to burn the chip with this message on it, but Tella discovers that the chip doesn't burn and she takes it. Then she sets off into the night to follow the chips instructions, which basically tell her to go to a city miles and miles away and pick an egg from a library.<br /><br />I swear, that's exactly what happens. The chip woman basically says, "So you're going to travel a few states to obtain an egg and race in a game of death," and Tella is basically, "lol okay." She follows the instructions of a woman on a chip, which her parents went to great lengths to destroy. This is Tella. This is our main character. <br /><br /><i>The last girl I see, I want to strangle. Like [someone she saw before], she has long hair. But instead of dark, it's blond -- no, honey gold -- and shines like that of a Broadway starlet. I can't see her eyes from here, but I'm sure they're some kind of stunning shade of blue. She has cream-colored skin and a body that belongs in a magazine -- the kind for guys, not girls. I hate her with everything I have as she laughs her perfect laugh and tosses her perfect hair and crosses her to-die-for legs. [...] We could be friends, I realize, if I weren't so overwhelmed with the urge to end her.</i><br /><br />That is also her. We're supposed to like her, mind you. Root for her to, you know, not die. Even though with everything we're given about her character, she should have tripped over a flat surface in the very beginning of the race and died.<br /><br /><i>I hate him.<br />The corner of his mouth quirks upward.<br />Or love him. </i><br /><br />And that is the romance. The few things I liked about this were the Digimon aspect (which, while obviously unoriginal, was a nice addition because Tella's Pandora was seriously adorable), and the writing, which was at times decent and funny. But that's it. This book makes no sense. There is no world-building, at all. The race isn't even over by the end of the novel. It's like, if your three-year-old were a big Hunger Games fan, and she drew a picture of Katniss, but it really looked like a raccoon with a crossbow that actually really looked somewhat phallic. That's Fire &amp; Flood. <br /><br />I'm really good at analogies. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14784890365595172817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review694115138">

<div id="review_753495524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/753495524" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/753495524?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer753495524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2968204046990718430">Does it bother you to think about being covered in bugs, bugs that eat your flesh and blood? Then prepare yourself because this book is nightmare-inducing! I'm not sure what it says about me to know that this is part of why I enjoyed it so much. I guess a book that can prompt such horrific images in my head to the point of making me shudder is up there with the awesome. Or maybe I should be on medication. That's up for debate. <br/><br/>Fire & Flood surprised me in many ways. At first it had a lot of simi</span>
  <span id="freeText2968204046990718430" style="display:none">Does it bother you to think about being covered in bugs, bugs that eat your flesh and blood? Then prepare yourself because this book is nightmare-inducing! I'm not sure what it says about me to know that this is part of why I enjoyed it so much. I guess a book that can prompt such horrific images in my head to the point of making me shudder is up there with the awesome. Or maybe I should be on medication. That's up for debate. <br><br>Fire &amp; Flood surprised me in many ways. At first it had a lot of similarities with The Hunger Games, which for me is a complete turn-off, so it's with pleasure that I can say these parallels fade early on, leaving us with an original, creative, and exciting novel. Ultimately we've got a survivalist story with dashes of fantastical and Sci-Fi elements. There are a lot of extreme conditions that we see Tella fight through, while making us wonder how we would do in her place. With cinematic details, each setting is brought to life from an endless yet claustrophobic jungle, to a dry, barren, and unbearably hot desert. It's all incredibly vivid. Which is both an applaud and a warning: I honestly felt those ants on me. For hours. Yes, it all comes back to the bugs. *shudders*<br><br>We meet a lot of characters throughout this story. With a large cast like this it's hard to connect to each character on an emotional level. This is not a huge problem seeing as this book is very plot driven. However it did leave a lot of room for me to analyze every single aspect of this story, to put what seemed like trivial details together, and eventually figuring out most of the many twists this book had up its sleeve. Still, some of them are clever, others creative, all leading to a very enjoyable read regardless of if you see them coming or not. The plot itself is full of secrets and conspiracies, giving us an interesting history behind this mysterious Brimstone Bleed - a race with a prize many would - and do - kill for. It involves some science fiction explanations that, I'm thinking, might be a hit or miss for some, but it brings about some really cool accessories (for lack of a better word and avoid spoiling) to help the contenders in the race. Actually one of my favorite parts was finding out what the Pandoras could do!<br><br>With uncomfortable conditions, hunger, anxiety, and fear throughout - oh, and ALL OF THE BUGS!! - Fire &amp; Flood will keep you in suspense from beginning to end!<br><br>I will leave you with this - ON YOUR FACE WHILE YOU SLEEP:<br><img height="200" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388700764i/7904957.png" width="173" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2968204046990718430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_835211859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/835211859" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/835211859?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer835211859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3303770058569222082">When I am given the opportunity to read a book that hasn’t been released yet, it means I am going into it without having been influenced by reading other reviews on Goodreads. It means going into it with no expectations, either positive or negative and leaving myself open to the possibility of finding a wonderful book. And that is exactly what happened when I read Fire and Flood by Victoria Scott. This is the first book I have read by Ms. Scott so I had no idea what to expect and what a surprise</span>
  <span id="freeText3303770058569222082" style="display:none">When I am given the opportunity to read a book that hasn’t been released yet, it means I am going into it without having been influenced by reading other reviews on Goodreads. It means going into it with no expectations, either positive or negative and leaving myself open to the possibility of finding a wonderful book. And that is exactly what happened when I read Fire and Flood by Victoria Scott. This is the first book I have read by Ms. Scott so I had no idea what to expect and what a surprise I was in for. I found this book to be fabulously exciting with a main character that surprised me at every turn. <br><br>Tella Holloway loved her life in Boston. Her idea of exercise was how far she would walk at the mall while shopping with her friends. But, her brother Cody has become ill with a mysterious disease. Countless Doctors have not been able to help him. Tella and Cody’s parents move them to a small town in Montana hoping the “quiet” life would be good for Cody. Tella misses her friends, internet, television, and all the comforts she has become so used to. Cody is slipping, getting weaker and weaker. Mysteriously, one night, Tella discovers a small gift box on her bed. In it is an invitation to participate in a race called the Brimstone Bleed. The winner of the race will receive a “cure” for their sick family member. What is this mysterious race? Who put the box on her bed? But Tella knows that whatever the answers to all her questions are, she has to go. She has to do whatever she can to try to save her brother. Thus starts an adventure that Tella never could have imagined.<br><br>The race is to take place in four sections, the jungle, desert, ocean and mountains. So Tella sets off with no idea what she is getting herself into. The first order of business is selecting a Pandora. The Pandora is an egg that will eventually hatch into an animal that will help them throughout their journey. Each animal is different, and each animal will have unique powers. Tella’s Pandora eventually ends up being a little black fox. But all the other animals obey their contenders. Tella’s doesn’t seem to listen to her at all. And what will it’s powers be? Does it even have any? No matter what, though, she loves her little fox and will do anything to protect it. <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/blackfox_zps321372a8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390957247i/8305611.jpg" alt=" photo blackfox_zps321372a8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The first part of the race is the jungle. A place where it rains all the time and you can hear strange things scurrying about in the darkness. Here Tella eventually meets up with some fellow contenders and they form a small group, deciding they are stronger together than alone. One person in particular is Guy. What is it about him that draws her to him? They form a tentative bond but this is a race. Only one person can win. Can she trust Guy, maybe even with her heart? <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/jungle_zpse3a3f01d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390957247i/8305612.jpg" alt=" photo jungle_zpse3a3f01d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>The second part of the race is the desert. Their little group has been through so much already. But the desert presents a whole new set of challenges. <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/desert_zpsee56bf85.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390957247i/8305613.jpg" alt=" photo desert_zpsee56bf85.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>I just can’t say enough great things about this book. Tella starts out as a typical teenager but during the course of the first two parts of this race she discovers so much about herself. She is so strong. But she is also so compassionate. She is not going to let this race harden her. She always does what she thinks is the right thing. Watching her change throughout the course of this book was so wonderful. And I loved watching her relationship with Guy change and grow. <br><br>As I said, this book takes us through the first two parts of the race so there are two left. As I was reading it, even if I had just a few minutes to grab a few pages throughout the day, I was immediately immersed back into this world. I could picture the deep greens of the jungle or the endless sand dunes of the desert. And the little black fox stole my heart right from the start. I can’t wait for the next book in this series. Thank you so much to NetGalley, Victoria Scott and Scholastic Press for giving me the opportunity to read this book.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3303770058569222082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102534643" />
    <a title="Jeff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17182481-jeff"><img alt="Jeff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480979507p2/17182481.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1102534643?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff" href="/user/show/17182481-jeff">Jeff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102534643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10864377969931629292">Very good indeed! Not my normal read but I enjoyed it thoroughly. I thought the pace was fantastic and something needs to be said about the increasing amount of new literature, that uses the short, sporadic chapter lengths. Some of the chapters in this book were 4 pages! I am used to epics which sometimes have chapters of 50 + pages, so having short chapters makes the book seem to fly by. Ultimately I fell in love with the story, and I will admit, the characters. I have a gripe against romance i</span>
  <span id="freeText10864377969931629292" style="display:none">Very good indeed! Not my normal read but I enjoyed it thoroughly. I thought the pace was fantastic and something needs to be said about the increasing amount of new literature, that uses the short, sporadic chapter lengths. Some of the chapters in this book were 4 pages! I am used to epics which sometimes have chapters of 50 + pages, so having short chapters makes the book seem to fly by. Ultimately I fell in love with the story, and I will admit, the characters. I have a gripe against romance in novels and this one is no exception, but I caught myself tolerating it a bit more in this one. It reminded me a bit of Philip Pullman's "his dark materials" trilogy with the usage of animal companions. So let's say an amalgamation of hunger games with his dark materials! Well done overall, very quick, very fast paced and very well written! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10864377969931629292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723984089?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723984089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16227577659753557957"><b>3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><blockquote>
<i>For a fleeting moment, before the woman speaks, I pray that the orange pack I’m wearing holds Chanel makeup. And a brush. And a mirror.</i> </blockquote><br/><br/>Welcome to the Prada sale of a lifetime, people! Instead of fighting past the Black Friday crowd for shoes, <b>the teenage <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9416.Confessions_of_a_Shopaholic?ac=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Becky Bloomwood</a></b> will take part in the Brimstone Bleed without makeup for a cure for her brother, Cody! She will be helped along by a steadfast, raised on Man vs Wild Luke 2.0! Join our heroes as they trek across jungles and deserts a</span>
  <span id="freeText16227577659753557957" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars </b><br><br><blockquote>
<i>For a fleeting moment, before the woman speaks, I pray that the orange pack I’m wearing holds Chanel makeup. And a brush. And a mirror.</i> </blockquote><br><br>Welcome to the Prada sale of a lifetime, people! Instead of fighting past the Black Friday crowd for shoes, <b>the teenage <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9416.Confessions_of_a_Shopaholic?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Becky Bloomwood</a></b> will take part in the Brimstone Bleed without makeup for a cure for her brother, Cody! She will be helped along by a steadfast, raised on Man vs Wild Luke 2.0! Join our heroes as they trek across jungles and deserts and ultimately end up with no resolution! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652574.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just as well, the cure probably wouldn't have matched Tella's nails.<br><br>I'm not the first person to point this out, but that doesn't mean I won't say it: <b>Fire &amp; Flood is a mash-up of The Hunger Games and Digimon.</b> A bunch of people have to compete under harsh conditions in order to save their loved ones and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the reason the Brimstone Bleed is being held is because of something their ancestors did just like the Districts' uprising. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> They get magical animals called Pandoras who are fiercely loyal to their Contender. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400234648i/9652575.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ah, the hours I wasted convincing my mom to buy me a Digivice. I never got one.<br><br>However, the protagonist is not a ruthless Katniss or a brave Tai, instead we get Tella, the American Becky Bloomwood.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652576.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Because I have no idea of what I’ll need, I also throw in random things from my desk: pens, paper, scissors, tape. The last thing I pack is a photo of my family that’s stuck in the edge of my mirror. That and my glittery purple nail polish.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Tella and I have a love-hate relationship because I definitely hated her in the beginning.</b> Victoria Scott explained in <a href="http://www.victoriascottya.com/addressing-femininity-young-adult-literature/" rel="nofollow noopener">her blog</a> that the reason she wrote Tella the way she is—girly and fixated on looks—was to give feminine characters a chance to shine. That's all very nice and well, and I heartily approve of Victoria's decision. There's no reason why you can't kick some zombie butt and then go pick out your prom dress right afterwards. <br><br>Tella goes way too far though. <b>She has exactly one hour to get to the train station and she wastes time by slicking on lip gloss.</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I think about how I should be racing toward Lincoln Station. But the compulsion to repair my face is too strong.<br><br>I grab my makeup bag — the one I never leave home without — and fix what I can.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399181233ra/9518848.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously, girl, <i>priorities</i>.<br><br>But I like what happens afterwards. Another Contender had used her silky tresses to gain the upper hand in a fight earlier, and Tella swallows her vanity and gives herself a haircut Mulan-style. It reminds me of that scene in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/204042.Naruto_Vol_01?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Naruto</a> where Sakura cuts her own hair short in order to be taken seriously as a ninja.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652577.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400234648i/9652578._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, whereas Sakura immediately whips out a kunai to fight after the dramatic hair-shoring, Tella laments her loss and comments on how her new hairstyle makes her eyes look wider and her lips fuller. And how her freckles stand out more.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652579.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One step at a time, I guess.<br><br><b>Did I mention that Tella can be incredibly stupid at times too?</b> A mysterious box shows up on her bed, telling her to participate in a competition to win a cure for Cody. Tella instantly packs up her bags (including her glittery nail polish) and hightails to the meeting place <b>without telling her parents</b>. You could argue that her mom suspected what was going on, but a note would be nice. Something like: <i>"Hey, mom and dad, I'm going to participate in this contest I know nothing about to win a maybe-non-existent cure for my dying brother. Toodles!</i> <br><br>For all Tella knows, this could be a scam and she could be sliced open for organs or something. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394582474ra/8874466.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She also falls prey to what I like to call the <b>Berners-Lee Cancellation Effect</b>. There's a computer at the diner Tella stops by, but she doesn't use it search up some information on what this Brimstone Bleed is before running blindly to the starting point. I don't even know why I'm bothering to point this out. <b>No one uses the Internet in YA novels.</b> We need to do research? Let's just <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937563905?type=review#rating_25392598" rel="nofollow noopener">go to a bar and ask random people!</a> It's not like there's this fantastic invention called Google or anything.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400234648i/9652580.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>See, even Becky-fucking-Bloomwood knows how to use Google!<br><br>Plus, for a girl who cares so much about looks, <b>Tella sure isn't shy about slut-shaming others.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The last girl I see, I want to strangle...she has long hair. But instead of dark, it's blond—no, honey gold—and shines like that of a Broadway starlet. I can't see her eyes from here, but I'm sure they're some kind of stunning shade of blue. She has cream-colored skin and a body that belongs in a magazine—the kind for guys, not girls. I hate her with everything I have as she laughs her perfect laugh and tosses her perfect hair and crosses her to-die-for legs...We could be friends, I realize, if I weren't so overwhelmed with the urge to end her.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>That's the girl who was desperately trying to beautify herself earlier. Even after Harper (that's the girl's name) lets Tella join her group for mutual protection and they become friends, she still relentlessly hates on Harper in her mind:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I'm relieved to see that she has the slightest hint of stretch marks on her belly. Though they're hardly visible, I'd like to imagine she was once enormous.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652581.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>How dare she be more beautiful than me and my purple nails! Fie!<br><br><b>Fortunately, Tella gets better in the second half.</b> I think Victoria Scott deliberately made Tella an annoying little whiner in the first half so when the character development fairy came, we'd be like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652582.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, it worked for me. Tella still has idiotic moments, including the shady <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825458283?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">rape culture</a> business with another Contender, but compared to the her before, Tella is a Katniss. She protects a bunch of stolen Pandoras from people who want to kill them. She fights back. She even <i>bites</i> someone who was attacking her. And this was the ditzy girl who was worrying about Chanel products.<br><br><b>Harper's by far my favorite character though.</b> She looks like a freaking supermodel, but is willing to sacrifice her looks for survival.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The bird raises a talon and makes a tiny slice three inches above her navel. Blood drips from the wound when the eagle removes her claw.<br>"Jesus, Harper," Levi says. "Couldn't you have used something besides your body?"<br>"My stomach is a map, see?" she explains, ignoring Levi. "When we find another flag, we make a new mark in relation to this one." Harper points at the bleeding cut. "It needs to always be with us," she says. But what she means is: me. It needs to always be with me. </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Now that's commitment. As Dumbledore said, scars are very useful. Tella could learn a thing or two from Harper.<br><br>Now for the setting, which I still haven't quite figured out. I know it's present-day because Tella mentioned Mcdonald's, Victoria's Secret and Lady Gaga. At the same time, there is some seriously advanced technology in form of fire-resistant radios and Pandoras. Lions can breathe fire. Eagles can turn invisible. Cute baby foxes can shapeshift.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yet no one questions this? They're totally cool with a raccoon being able to heal wounds with a flick of its tongue? If it were me, I'd freak out, slaughter my way to the top and then figure out how to turn this baby into cash.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400234648i/9652584.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>What, Cassie Clare's doing it.<br><br>All in all, Fire &amp; Flood isn't a bad read. The heroine might get on your nerves at first, but her ditzy monologues are quite funny sometimes and her character develops as the book goes on. And Madox, Tella's Pandora, is freaking <i>adorable</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400234648ra/9652585.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I need a Pandora, stat.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940434773" rel="nofollow noopener">My Review of Salt &amp; Stone</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16227577659753557957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_681871362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681871362" />
    <a title="Paula Stokes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5630039-paula-stokes"><img alt="Paula Stokes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408899590p2/5630039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681871362?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula Stokes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula Stokes" href="/user/show/5630039-paula-stokes">Paula Stokes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681871362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1685192369686421560">The Hunger Games meets The Amazing Race meets How to Train Your Dragon, and the result is freaking outstanding.<br/><br/>Sixteen-year-old Tella is just an ordinary girl with extraordinary problems. Her older brother is dying of a mysterious illness and the only way she can save him is to enter an epic race across desert, jungle, mountain, and ocean. Tella's not much of an outdoorswoman--her idea of roughing it is going without internet access--but not trying means letting her brother die, and that ain't h</span>
  <span id="freeText1685192369686421560" style="display:none">The Hunger Games meets The Amazing Race meets How to Train Your Dragon, and the result is freaking outstanding.<br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Tella is just an ordinary girl with extraordinary problems. Her older brother is dying of a mysterious illness and the only way she can save him is to enter an epic race across desert, jungle, mountain, and ocean. Tella's not much of an outdoorswoman--her idea of roughing it is going without internet access--but not trying means letting her brother die, and that ain't happening. And so begins the Brimstone Bleed.<br /><br />What I liked best about Fire &amp; Flood (other than the Pandoras--I want one of those almost as much as my letter from Hogwarts) is the balance displayed. Tella is tough, but still very relatable. Although she's trapped in an inhospitable environment with her life constantly in danger, I never felt like her plight was hopeless. With a less deft hand, this story could have become overly bleak, but Victoria Scott uses her supporting characters and their Pandora companions to infuse laughter and lightness at just the right moments. <br /><br />Fire &amp; Flood is an epic adventure story full of high-stakes action and just the right amount of humor and romance. I laughed. I swooned. I cheered. I got angry. I cried. I cheered some more. Readers will want to root for Tella as she embraces her newfound inner strength and risks everything to save her brother. <br /><br />Sometimes you don't know what you want in a book until you read one that hits all the marks. For me, this book was PERFECT. I eagerly await the next installment...and the arrival of my Pandora egg ;-)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1685192369686421560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
