<div id="review_1420965059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420965059" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1420965059?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420965059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4504758149363129131"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>So I was loving the beginning of the book because Tella was so funny with her snark. Then... she gets the little ear piece thingy that says she can join the Brimstone Bleed if she gets to so and so by so and so time. <br/><br/>There are things about the book I liked and others were just:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447456808i/17007191._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I loved when Tella got there, got her egg and got on with where they had to start the game. And I fell in love with her Pandora, which comes from the egg they get in the beginning, he wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4504758149363129131" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br><br>So I was loving the beginning of the book because Tella was so funny with her snark. Then... she gets the little ear piece thingy that says she can join the Brimstone Bleed if she gets to so and so by so and so time. <br><br>There are things about the book I liked and others were just:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447456808i/17007191._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved when Tella got there, got her egg and got on with where they had to start the game. And I fell in love with her Pandora, which comes from the egg they get in the beginning, he was a little fox, but he has some things he can do :) <br><br>I loved Guy, he ended up being Tella's love interest and his pandora was a lion. <br><br>The thing is a few of them team up to help each other get to the finish line. They start out in the jungle and a few people and pandora's die attempting to get to their destination in two weeks. <br><br>There is a guy that is a jerk and a half, his name is Titus. He is evil to the core and I wanted someone to take him out.. maybe they do...<br><br>Anyhoo, over all I liked the book but I didn't love it like I thought I would from the start. Makes me sad because... well because it just does! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447456808ra/17007192.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm glad there are many out there that loved it though, there is nothing like loving a book :) I don't like the meh ones or the ones I really don't like at all..... Fin<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4504758149363129131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_434854906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/434854906" />
    <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist"><img alt="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445582024p2/5383215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/434854906?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist">Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist?shelf=book-looks">book-looks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434854906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16303216341585079929"><blockquote>If you’re hearing this message, you are invited to be a Contender in the Brimstone Bleed. All Contenders must report within forty-eight hours to select their Pandora companions. If you do not appear within forty-eight hours, your invitations will be eliminated.<br/>The Brimstone Bleed will last three months and will take place across four ecosystems: desert, sea, mountains, jungle. The winning prize will be the Cure—a remedy for any illness, for any single person.<br/>There will only be one champion.”</blockquote><br/>I’ve</span>
  <span id="freeText16303216341585079929" style="display:none"><blockquote>If you’re hearing this message, you are invited to be a Contender in the Brimstone Bleed. All Contenders must report within forty-eight hours to select their Pandora companions. If you do not appear within forty-eight hours, your invitations will be eliminated.<br>The Brimstone Bleed will last three months and will take place across four ecosystems: desert, sea, mountains, jungle. The winning prize will be the Cure—a remedy for any illness, for any single person.<br>There will only be one champion.”</blockquote><br>I’ve been looking forward to Fire &amp; Flood since it was first announced and before it even had a cover. I fell in love with The Collector and was eager for more from Victoria Scott! Even though this isn’t my usual kind of book, but I didn’t care. I was excited to meet Tella and Guy (!) and the Pandoras. My favorite aspect of The Collector, was how Victoria captured Dante’s voice so perfectly. I was curious to see how Tella’s character would be since she’s worlds away from Dante. From the first page, I knew Tella and I would get along just fine. This girl was funny and witty with such an awesome sarcastic attitude. The fact that she’s also fearless and determined to save her brother at all costs, makes it pretty much impossible to not love this girl.<br><br>Tella’s older brother has a rare, undiagnosed and incurable diseases that is slowly killing him. It broke my heart to see how determined Tella and her brother are to keep their relationship the same, even if he can’t even get out of bed anymore. When Tella receives a mysterious message telling her she has 48 hours to report to be a contestant to the Brimstone Bleed. Winning the race will get her the cure for her brother’s illness, but there can only be one winner. Tella has no other option, she knows she’s her brother’s only option so she sets off to try to save his life. I was so excited for the Pandora selection and to see what animal Tella (and the other contenders) got to help her in the race. This was one of my favorite parts of the book and as much as I loved the story, the Pandoras kind of stole the show. No I won’t spoil what Pandora Tella chooses, or what his name is or what he can do. But I will tell you that you will love him as much as Tella does.<br><br>The competition, Brimstone Bleed, last three months and covers different ecosystems: desert, jungle, etc. This takes up a good chunk of the book and kept my attention the entire time. Tella meets other contenders who are also competing for a cure for a loved one. She even befriends a group of them. I think this is one of the reasons why the competition part of the book never gets boring. It’s not just Tella wondering by herself (although she does for a bit in the beginning) but we get to meet this great cast of secondary characters. My favorite was Harper, who I wasn’t even sure I would like when I first met her. But of course, my favorite character was Guy Chambers. *insert dreamy sigh here* *and another one* If I were to go to the Brimstone Bleed, I would pick Guy Chambers as my Pandora ;) This is one of those slow-building relationships, but the payoff is worth it! I was hooked on Tella and Guy’s every interactions. So excited to see where this goes next!<br><br>While I’ve heard the comparisons between this and Hunger Games, other than the competition thing, I didn’t really see it. It was like when people would compare every vampire book to Twilight…For me, it was more like an awesome mix of The Amazing Race and Pokemon. Pandora, I choose you!!! This is part of a series so there will definitely be unanswered questions in the end, but I do love the way everything came together at the end and gave us the perfect set up for book two. The ending wasn’t a cliffhanger (at least not for me) but it does end in a to-be-continued sort of way that will have you itching to get your hands on the next book. A thrilling and action-packed story with vivid descriptions and plot twists (some you may expect and some that will blindside you), Fire &amp; Flood will take you on an epic adventure!<br><br>4.5 out of 5 stars!<br><br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/nereyda1003/media/Book%20Looks/blfireampflood_zps19ac8fbd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383438307i/6558559.jpg" alt=" photo blfireampflood_zps19ac8fbd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://www.polyvore.com/fire_flood/set?.embedder=8312598&amp;.svc=copypaste&amp;id=99986570" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire &amp; Flood</a> by <a target="_blank" href="http://nereyda1003.polyvore.com/?.embedder=8312598&amp;.svc=copypaste" rel="nofollow noopener">nereyda1003</a><br><br>***<br>Read full review &amp; more of my reviews at <a href="http://www.mostlyyabookobsessed.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Mostly YA Book Obsessed</a><br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/albums/u367/nereyda1003/?action=view&amp;current=MyBlogSignature.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349417i/703417.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16303216341585079929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_594574520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/594574520" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594574520?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781909489622" href="/book/show/18628138-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=bleh">bleh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=could-have-been-so-much-better">could-have-been-so-much-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594574520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4190025293561344377">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>1.5 stars</b><br/><br/>After the endless praise and fangirling for the<em> Dante Walker</em> series, I was hoping Fire & Flood would deliver correspondingly. Instead, I got a cheap version of The Hunger Games with a dash of Pokemon.<br/><br/>No second thoughts aside, Fire & Flood was lacking originality. We got a pin, an Effie-replica, a rush to the Cornucopia (but this time for eggs). The main character's motive to enter the game was to save her sibling, the competitors were thrown into an </span>
  <span id="freeText4190025293561344377" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br><br><b>1.5 stars</b><br><br>After the endless praise and fangirling for the<em> Dante Walker</em> series, I was hoping Fire &amp; Flood would deliver correspondingly. Instead, I got a cheap version of The Hunger Games with a dash of Pokemon.<br><br>No second thoughts aside, Fire &amp; Flood was lacking originality. We got a pin, an Effie-replica, a rush to the Cornucopia (but this time for eggs). The main character's motive to enter the game was to save her sibling, the competitors were thrown into an unknown environment and there will be only one winner. There's even this:<br><blockquote>"I'd like to officially welcome you to the Brimstone Bleed. May the bravest Contender win."</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400586430ra/9692258.gif" alt="" width="410" height="272" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>However it wasn't just the glaringly alike symbols and characters that put me off. The biggest party-pooper was the main character. To put it candidly, Tella is vain and every other synonym for stupid. When she finds a mysterious device that gives her instructions, she listens to it. She doesn't care about if it's just a prank or could lead her to danger, she listens to it because it just <em>seems</em> right--even though her parents tried to burn the device. Then she leaves her home without informing her parents. Well, aren't you just the most considerate and brightest kid! Then, in the race, she frets about her appearance and not taking makeup with her. GIRL. YOU NEED FOOD AND SHELTER. NOT MAKEUP. *rips face apart in frustration*<br><blockquote>The last girl I see, I want to strangle. [...] I can't see her eyes from here, but I'm sure they're some kind of stunning shade of blue. She has cream-colored skin and a body that belongs in a magazine--the kind for guys, not girls. I hate her with everything I have as she laughs her perfect laugh and tosses her perfect hair and crosses her to-die-for legs. [...] We could be friends, I realise, if I weren't so overwhelmed with the urge to end her.</blockquote><br>*rips out organs* That quote speaks for itself.<br><br>I can't even talk about the romance. It was disastrous and pointless and ridiculous on so many levels. There wasn't instant love, but the love interest was so unappealing, like the main character. Was Fire &amp; Flood written by the same author as <em>Dante Walker</em>? Because I'm struggling to believe it.<br><br>I can say nothing positive about the world building. What is there to say where there was barely much of it? We got a few basic facts, but I wanted to know more. More, in order to understand Tella's world and actually become engrossed into the book. Instead, I was standing on the sidelines, only seeing half of what could have been an amazing and unique world.<br><br>The only thing that made Fire &amp; Flood bearable were the Pandoras. I found them to be rather interesting and a lot of fun to learn about. Putting it simply, they are animal companions that hatch out of the eggs and have special abilities, they help the competitors during the competition and each and every one of them are unique.<br><br>To sum up, Fire &amp; Flood was a huge disappointment. Originality is one thing, but unlikable and weakly developed characters just were enough.<br><p>
  <em>~Thank you Scholastic Australia for sending me this copy!~</em>
</p> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4190025293561344377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_645043542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645043542" />
    <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers"><img alt="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384217885p2/14564026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645043542?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers">Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=a-must-read">a-must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=you-ll-be-sorry-if-you-miss-this-bo">you-ll-be-sorry-if-you-miss-this-bo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=fav-s">fav-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=can-t-wait-for-the-sequel">can-t-wait-for-the-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645043542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13981098930294295716"><br/><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Oh, where do I even begin? FIRE & FLOOD amazed me!! Seriously, I was not expecting FIRE & FLOOD to be as amazing as it was! It is definitely a "MUST READ OF 2014!"<br/><br/>I have to admit, the beginning drove me insane! The main character Tella, was SO annoying, whinny and the most childish Main Character that I have read, maybe even ever! BUT, as the book progressed and Tella actually found out that there was a way to save her brother, she changed. She became determined, stronger, motivated, an</span>
  <span id="freeText13981098930294295716" style="display:none"><br /><b>4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Oh, where do I even begin? FIRE &amp; FLOOD amazed me!! Seriously, I was not expecting FIRE &amp; FLOOD to be as amazing as it was! It is definitely a "MUST READ OF 2014!"<br /><br />I have to admit, the beginning drove me insane! The main character Tella, was SO annoying, whinny and the most childish Main Character that I have read, maybe even ever! BUT, as the book progressed and Tella actually found out that there was a way to save her brother, she changed. She became determined, stronger, motivated, and SO much less annoying! She became a fighter! It's like she became a totally different person all together. Granted she still had her occasional sixteen year old moments, but she knew what needed to be done, and she knew whining about them was not going to take her over the finish line. And she even started cracking me up about half through the book! I was laughing pretty much every other paragraph! I mean she was saying the most stupidest/funniest things, and I'm thinking "When the hell did Tella become a comedian because this girl is seriously cracking me up?" But I also came to see why it was important for Tella to be the way she was in the beginning. What fun would it of been if we had this baddass, tough chick from the beginning? Well yeah, that might of been great. But I think it was important to see Tella as she was; a normal sixteen year old girl, whining about hair and nail polish. Then to watch her as she was willing to throw it all away to save her brother, and grow into a strong, determined young adult, who will endure anything to save the one she loves! Tella really became an amazing character by the end of the book. And I came to appreciate her in the beginning because of who she became at the end! Does that make since? <br /><br /><b>THE PLOT...</b><br /><br />What would you do to save the one you love? Would you go to any limit for a chance of bringing the one you love back to good health? Would you battle the most brutal environments just to compete for a slim chance to get a cure for the one you love? Would you be willing to kill someone if need be, in-order to survive and bring home the cure?<br /><br />Well that's exactly what Tella and every other contender in The Brimstone Bleed is prepared to do in-order to save the one they love!<br /><br />Tella, a Sixteen year old girl is determined to find a way to save her brother from the disease eating away at his body. And the only chance she has is competing in a vicious race against a hundred or so more contenders, all there for the same thing, The CURE! <br /><br />Every contender is given the opportunity to save a love one. They've been invited into the Brimstone Bleed, where contenders will race through 4 ecosystems: Jungle, Desert, Mountains, and Sea. They will be forced to endure the harsh environments with very limited resources. But luckily, every contender enters the race with a Pandora egg, which will later hatch and in essence become their only life line in the race! Their Pandora animal is special, not like regular animals, and they will have to rely on their Pandora's if their going to have any chance of winning this race or even surviving period!<br /><br />The race is on, and their can only be ONE winner out of so many! But after each ecosystem is completed, the winner of that particular ecosystem will be granted a small prize and given the opportunity to return home if they wish. But there is ONLY one winner that will win the complete cure to save one single person, and everyone is there to save someone they love, and most are willing to do just about ANY thing to win the race and get the Cure!<br /><br />Tella will face many obstacles and hardships along the way. But she teams up with a group of other contenders all agreed to travel together until the final leg of the race, then it will be every man for themselves. But Tella can't help to feel close to her group and want to help them, not make it harder for them, for the ecosystems does that enough. But there is one particular boy that looks at her as she is different. He is distant, and rough around the edges, but something about this boy is pulling her closer and closer to him. But what will happen when the time comes to battle her friends for the cure? Will she be able to do what needs to be done when the time comes for every man to stand on there own? <br /><br />FIRE &amp; FLOOD is a book that is NOT to be missed! It satisfies all cravings for, action, adventure, blood-shed, survival, betrayal, love, and of course romance! <br /><br /><b>Victoria Scott, PLEASE bring on the next one, because I will be holding my breath until then!!!</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13981098930294295716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_863790884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863790884" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863790884?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=sci-fi-alicious">sci-fi-alicious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863790884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4762131031348726530">Someone much crueller than me would describe this book as a Survivor Reality show meets YA. Giant race, one winner, only instead of a cash prize and not-so-eternal glory, the winner of the Brimstone Bleed gets a cure to save their dying relative. That’s the situation every contestant, including Tella our protagonist, is in.<br/><br/>With only their Pandoras to rely on, each contender has to run the game with no rules and make it to the finish line first to claim a prize. Fire & Flood covers the first two </span>
  <span id="freeText4762131031348726530" style="display:none">Someone much crueller than me would describe this book as a Survivor Reality show meets YA. Giant race, one winner, only instead of a cash prize and not-so-eternal glory, the winner of the Brimstone Bleed gets a cure to save their dying relative. That’s the situation every contestant, including Tella our protagonist, is in.<br><br>With only their Pandoras to rely on, each contender has to run the game with no rules and make it to the finish line first to claim a prize. Fire &amp; Flood covers the first two locations, half of the race, and follows Tella as she tries to survive the harsh conditions to save her brother. Clearly my first thought was to seriously consider whether I would do such a race for either of my brothers.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394311770ra/8834724.gif" alt="haha no" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Should have let me play with your lego, asshole!</i><br><br>Honestly, I’m joking. Pretty sure I’d do this at least once for each of my brosephs, but maybe that’s because I think I could probably survive this whole experience a bit better than Tella who has exactly no survival skills. Tella, I love you, but you roll a leech off. Don’t pull it! Basically, the only thing stopping me from winning this race would be my appalling sense of direction.<br><br>Scott had completely won me over with The Collector, so I was pretty excited to read this. It is a massive departure in style, story and thematically which is brave of Scott as a writer to embrace. I have a lot of respect for authors who can branch out and try new things. This book mostly worked for me. I didn’t absolutely love it, but I quite liked it.<br><br>The positives are what Scott brought to the table in terms of characterisation. The book is very character driven when not drowning you in suspense and walking. The survivalist aspects of the novel are a major selling point if you’re into that sort of thing. But I would have liked to have seen more development in the romance. What did Guy like about Tella? What made them click other than throbbing hormones and the safety net he provides her? I couldn’t say. Not that I didn’t like Guy but that their relationship made little sense to me.<br><br>The Pandoras are a great addition to the novel, providing much of the moral quandary and entertainment for the reader. Scott has pulled all out to build up not just the cast, but their Pokemon sidekicks too, in order to enrich the novel. Downside is that the story just didn’t make much sense. The eventual explanation for the race was something of an anticlimax, leaving me scratching my head and wondering how this event has stayed so incognito. There’s a lot of questions and not nearly enough answers.<br><br>All up it was an enjoyable novel and I look forward to the sequel. Even if I could beat this book in a race.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394311770i/8834725.jpg" alt="man vs wild" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4762131031348726530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_917813403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917813403" />
    <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads"><img alt="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566850655p2/16219087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/917813403?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_574771844" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574771844" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574771844?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">readers who have survived their fair share of Shoujo Anime/Manga</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=on-going-series">on-going-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=welcome-to-the-jungle-beach-island">welcome-to-the-jungle-beach-island</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574771844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3305545944471562303"><i>
  <b>2.5 STARS<br/><blockquote>There's a part of me that doesn't like her considering us tools in this race. I just want… for these people to be my friends.</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>Take that as fair warning should you decide to pick this one up. Also:<br/><br/>Do NOT expect The Hunger Games' depth.<br/><br/>Do NOT look for Dante Walker's charming snark.<br/><br/>Do NOT expect to like the heroine. Only a few will get this analogy but she's Miaka from <i>Fushigi Yuugi</i> with a cuddly <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[wolf-like <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <i>Pokemon</i> shoved to survive a <i>Lord of the Flies</i>/<i>The </i></span>
  <span id="freeText3305545944471562303" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>2.5 STARS<br><blockquote>There's a part of me that doesn't like her considering us tools in this race. I just want… for these people to be my friends.</blockquote></b>
</i><br>Take that as fair warning should you decide to pick this one up. Also:<br><br>Do NOT expect The Hunger Games' depth.<br><br>Do NOT look for Dante Walker's charming snark.<br><br>Do NOT expect to like the heroine. Only a few will get this analogy but she's Miaka from <i>Fushigi Yuugi</i> with a cuddly <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[wolf-like <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <i>Pokemon</i> shoved to survive a <i>Lord of the Flies</i>/<i>The Amazing Race</i> hybrid of a predicament in order to win a cure for her sickly older brother Cody.<br><br>Her name is Tella Holloway. She now lives in Montana with her parents, transplanted from Boston because her brother is sick. Like going to die eventually sick. She receives a listening device that tells her she has been selected to be a Contender in the Brimstone Bleed, a race where the ultimate prize is the ultimate cure for her brother's ultimately unnamed ailment. Which of course she joins because A) that's what you do when these strange circumstances happen to you and B) she's bored as hell in Montana.<br><br>Oh alright, she also cares for her brother and wants him to live long and prosper. Plus mom gave her a lucky feather to wear which would be totally bizarre outside the context of a strange mysterious race.<br><br>Anyway, contingent to joining this race is that she has to choose a Pandora to accompany and help her. At the beginning of the story the participants come into a house with eggs that eventually hatch into curious creatures with special abilities meant to protect and help them make it through the dire conditions of the contest. The Brimstone Bleed will last for three months where they are directed to find the base camp in each of four ecosystems: jungle, desert, mountains and sea with each leg yielding a winner, earning them a minor prize and a choice. As with how most of this stories go, other Contenders and their own Pandoras get incorporated in Tella's quest: a gorgeous amazonian blonde (Harper), redhead twin boys (Levi and Ransom), an unlikely pair of a middle aged woman (Caroline) and a young boy (Dink), the cruel sinister boy (Titus) and the ruthlessly methodical young man who seem to know more about the race than he lets on (Guy).<br><br>The thing is, <i>Fire &amp; Flood</i> had an interesting story to tell. I like that it isn't entirely a rehash of what THG set out to accomplish and had some original ideas in the Pandoras and okay, an unlikely heroine. I like the imagination and personality behind the creatures the most and I do appreciate the effort to give the readers something different, despite the feeling that their sole purpose was to manipulate me into liking Tella by proximity.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390965048ra/8307209.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It took me a bit of time trying to figure out what Victoria Scott is trying to cut across writing her lead character like Tella. There was very shallow character build up in the beginning for this heroine. It feels like carrying out a personal conversation with a complete stranger who talk as if you're BFFs right off the bat. Which of course rubbed me the wrong way because you know, introduce yourself first, FFS. That's what rational people are inclined to do after all.<br><br>So I get dragged into this "adventure" with a virtual stranger who gradually starts to grate on my nerves with her observations, her godawful singing meant to be interpreted as cute (I HATE any form of singing when its done out of context. The only context acceptable being: drunk in a karaoke bar or forced at gun-point.) then it clicks: she's a shoujo anime heroine! The ditzy, clueless, goofy and hokey type trying to survive while away from her usual comforts but is going to kick everyone's ass down the line. One can hope.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>The only thing I can think while I'm swallowing a hunk of snake is that I am the type of person to have three glittery feather boas draped over my dresser mirror at home: purple, pink and red. And now I am eating a snake.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390965048ra/8307210.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I could get down with that. I mean I survived (half of) Sailormoon and Fushigi Yuugi (the entirety WITH OAVs) this will be great.<br><br>Then she jumped into that swamp-river to save a drowning woman (without good cause, probably screaming <b>"Too kawaii to live, too sugoi to die!"</b> while doing it) who got saved by an eight year old boy instead… leaving Tella as the new other victim the rest of the group has to save.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390965048ra/8307211.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm fine with ditzy so long as there's some counterpoint to the ditzy in the heroine's character. Unfortunately this had barely there counterpoint. More than the humor that fell this side of flat, Tella's more of a spectator than a doer. Or if she does anything its towards the ends of being the victim to be saved instead and make allowances for by everyone around her. She WATCHES. Not in the voyeuristic sense but in the I'm-an-innocent-bystander-in-a-chaotic-hotel-lobby sense. Someone in the group starts to vomit? She CALLS someone to attend to the person. She wakes up realizing she's sleeping on a bed while the rest are sleeping on the floor? She goes back to sleep. And so on and so forth. But when she decides to meddle its out of impulse with catastrophic consequences.<br><br>It's like an infinite well of effort NOT to redeem her.<br><br>Such that in the second half of the book when some effort was exerted to present her in a more favorable light, the aftertaste of her earlier behavior just refuses to wash out. There was no adorbs, her antics just sends my eyes to roll seismically particularly with the introduction of that WTF romantic angle. I suppose having someone muscled and tattooed in the story, it was bound to happen. <br><br>Guy as a hero was all about the knuckle cracking, cliche dishing and intense gazing. Beyond that… well he has a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[fire-breathing lion for a Pandora <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> so he has that working out for him. So yeah, I guess yay, Guy-Tella! (I have a sudden hankering for Nutella.)<br><br>I do have an issue with Guy keeping his secret for the majority of the book. Because <b>WHY?</b> There was no burden really on him to keep that from everyone else. Or if there is I don't get it. I also spent the great majority of this book nitpicking the details of the Brimstone Bleed: because overanalyzing me is having an issue with a Contender racing to save someone dying of Alcoholic Liver Cirrhosis versus someone racing to save a child born with unresectable Rhabdomyosarcoma. Fortunately it was explained, though rather insubstantially with lots of logic and motivational holes. Unfortunately its at the very end.<br><br>I did like some of the reveals towards the end, though the entire scene in the last sequence came across shoddy and rather messy. People were turning up out of nowhere, damning temporal continuity and circumstance. Jaxon and Olivia's introduction late in the story made them out as token additions. Emotional manipulation was on full blast with the last instruction in the race. Something I can forgive as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really did like the Pandoras <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>I am reluctant to continue with this series because on the one hand the ending holds some promise to expanding the intriguing premise of the Brimstone Bleed, maybe some potential to create better complexity in the race itself.<br><br>On the other, there's Tella.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I'm just a girl who loves purple and Greek food and mani-pedis and singing out of tune. A girl who would give almost anything to be away from here and magically back in Boston, hanging out with her best friend, Hannah. I'm just a girl who thought she could save her brother.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390965048ra/8307212.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/774770/too-kawaii-to-live-too-sugoi-to-die" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on BookLikes.</a><br><br><i>ARC provided by Scholastic Press thru Netgalley in exchange for an honest unbiased review. Quotes may not appear on the final edition.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3305545944471562303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5193512-whitley-birks?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5193512-whitley-birks?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer861170300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16831207082410947673">I GIVE UP.<br/><br/>I SURRENDER.<br/><br/>JUST ANYTHING TO STOP GOING THROUGH THIS BOOK.<br/><br/>This wasn't even the worst book I've gone through on my blog, but that just contributed to its utter boredom. There wasn't even (much) for me to rag on. It was just bland event after bland event, all of it poorly described, with no context, no detail, and <i>no consequences</i>. Tella gets a rash, then forgets about. Tella gets chased by monkeys, then after they're gone never mentions them again. Tella gets an illogical ever-bleeding w</span>
  <span id="freeText16831207082410947673" style="display:none">I GIVE UP.<br /><br />I SURRENDER.<br /><br />JUST ANYTHING TO STOP GOING THROUGH THIS BOOK.<br /><br />This wasn't even the worst book I've gone through on my blog, but that just contributed to its utter boredom. There wasn't even (much) for me to rag on. It was just bland event after bland event, all of it poorly described, with no context, no detail, and <i>no consequences</i>. Tella gets a rash, then forgets about. Tella gets chased by monkeys, then after they're gone never mentions them again. Tella gets an illogical ever-bleeding wound that she rubs germs into, and then it's completely forgotten. Tella jumps in a river, almost drowns, and sprains her ankle, but after she runs on it for a while she's perfectly fine and it's never mentioned again. Horrific, brain-breaking stereotypes appear to try and kill everyone for completely unexplained reasons, and then they vanish and no one talks about them again.<br /><br />That's it. That's the whole book. Things that could be interesting, described in an absolute minimum of detail and never having any result at all. The whole thing is just a series of vague actions that add up to fuck-all nothing because they don't even add.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16831207082410947673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1200756746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200756746" />
    <a title="Joelle (Throne of books) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17660097-joelle-throne-of-books"><img alt="Joelle (Throne of books) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587611161p2/17660097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200756746?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joelle (Throne of books) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joelle (Throne of books) " href="/user/show/17660097-joelle-throne-of-books">Joelle (Throne of books) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200756746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15349149941293092986">*Read March 2014* <br/>The Hunger Games meets Pokémon in this addictive new series about a race against jungle and desert!<br/> Tella Holloway's brother is sick. When the doctors can't determine what's wrong, Tella's family moves to Montana for a change of scenery and fresh they hope will help her brother. One day Tella receives a mysterious box with an earpiece giving her instructions to become a contender in the Brimstone Bleed. It's an epic race against Jungle and desert, that will help her win the cur</span>
  <span id="freeText15349149941293092986" style="display:none">*Read March 2014* <br />The Hunger Games meets Pokémon in this addictive new series about a race against jungle and desert!<br /> Tella Holloway's brother is sick. When the doctors can't determine what's wrong, Tella's family moves to Montana for a change of scenery and fresh they hope will help her brother. One day Tella receives a mysterious box with an earpiece giving her instructions to become a contender in the Brimstone Bleed. It's an epic race against Jungle and desert, that will help her win the cure she needs to help her brother. The only problem is, all the contenders are after the cure. <br /> Everyone buckle up and get ready for the intense roller coaster ride that is this first installment in a new series! <br /> I must say I was genuinely surprised by how much this blew my mind. It's Very similar to The Hunger Games with a Pokemon twist to it. The "Pandoras" are the companions that follow the contenders along on their race for the cure and I was stunned to find out that they are unique in that they have abilities. Such as Fire breathing, and invisibility. <br /> The main character, Tella, is perhaps the most relatable character I've ever read about. Can't run off into a race without our glittery nail polish! She's smart, funny, and most importantly, Human. So many other authors tries to make their main characters seem invincible with super bad-ass skills but Victoria Scott has written a character who is like us, a simple teenage girl who tries her best and gives it her all rather than be someone who is an unbelievably skilled badass right off the first page. The character development was SO beautifully executed, I really felt a connection between the main character and me, I loved Guy (the love interest) who started off being borderline rude but as you read on you learn that's a just a front he puts up. The Pandoras were also very importantly a huge part of the story. The world building went along smoothly, it was so well described I could vividly picture everything in my head, it was crystal clear. <br /> Also Titus was very well hated. HARPER MY LOVE. MY HEART GOES OUT TO HER. ILY HARPER. Okay I'll stop talking about all the characters now or I'll never stop. <br />Full of heart warming moments, heartbreaking moments and twists and turns you never saw coming! Fire &amp; Flood is an instant new favorite and I can not recommend it enough, I HIGHLY suggest you go and buy this book right now. And yes, I'm being bossy. Do I care? NO! This book was too good to be ignored by you! GO. BUY. THIS. BOOK.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15349149941293092986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_675582430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/675582430" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/675582430?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=actiony">actiony</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer675582430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4895936562840284045"><b>Whoa, what a wild ride!</b><br/><br/>I have seen other reviewers say that this book is like a mix between The Hunger Games and The Amazing Race, and yeah, I can absolutely see that! The thrills and excitement are non stop as we follow a very special girl through an extraordinary journey.<br/><br/>16 year old Tella has been dragged out to the middle of Montana by her parents. Her older brother, Cody, is sick with a mysteriously degenerating disease, and they felt that the fresh air would be good for him. Now Tella is wi</span>
  <span id="freeText4895936562840284045" style="display:none"><b>Whoa, what a wild ride!</b><br /><br />I have seen other reviewers say that this book is like a mix between The Hunger Games and The Amazing Race, and yeah, I can absolutely see that! The thrills and excitement are non stop as we follow a very special girl through an extraordinary journey.<br /><br />16 year old Tella has been dragged out to the middle of Montana by her parents. Her older brother, Cody, is sick with a mysteriously degenerating disease, and they felt that the fresh air would be good for him. Now Tella is without her friends, without technology, being home schooled by her mother, and is watching her brother slowly die. She deals with the lack of a real life as best she can, but her situation is not awesome. <br /><br />Everything changes when she discovers a mysterious blue box on her bed which contains an invitation for her to become a Contender in the ‘Brimstone Bleed’ - a three-month long race across jungle, desert, ocean and mountains – with the winner receiving a Cure for one person, for any illness. Tella loves her brother deeply, so she doesn’t even have to think twice when she decides to sneak away from her family and follow the bizarre instructions she receives in order to enter the race. <br /><br />What follows is a thrilling, non-stop adventure as Tella is thrown into the race of her life. With only a ‘Pandora’ by her side (no, I’m not telling you what that is, you’ll just have to read and discover, because it’s all a little bit awesome), she is one of 120+ Contenders in the Brimstone Bleed – first stop – jungle. <br /><br />Tella allies with a bunch of Contenders – a fantastic group of characters including children that will steal your heart, smartass teenage twins, a few smartass 20-somethings, and, a deeply mysterious, super-hot Bear Grylls-type character who brings a nice element of badassery and heart-pounding awesome to the story. All racing to save somebody that they love, their group must face the perils of their environment, as well as others racing for the same goal. <br /><br />Going in, I wasn’t quite sure what to expect from this book. And whatever you do, don’t go in expecting another Hunger Games, yes there are elements that are similar, but this book is different in so many ways. Mainly – it’s not dystopian. It’s set in the modern day, in the real world, nobody has superpowers, and the Brimstone Bleed isn’t something that everybody knows about. It seems to be a secret, and that’s all part of the mystery – where are they, why are they racing, who organised it, why do they have a cure, and why are there so many people sick in the first place?<br /><br />I was hooked from the very first page. I instantly loved Tella! She is a normal girl who loves her brother fiercely, and her bravery and determination to help him is incredible. She also has a sensational sense of humour, and I laughed out loud so many times while reading! Even while she’s in the <i>“epicentre of hell”</i>, she remains true to herself, she doesn’t fall apart, and her monologue is just brilliant. <br /><br /><blockquote>“<i>For some reason, the only thing I can think while I’m swallowing a hunk of snake is that I am the type of person to have three glittery feather boas draped over my dresser mirror at home, purple, pink, and red. And now I am eating snake.</i>”</blockquote><br />With all of the intensity going on around her, this was a very welcome part of the storyline. Tella’s monologue is like a breath of fresh air, and even though she is stressed out, facing death and danger, she is still a bit of a smartass, and I love it!<br /><br /><blockquote>“<i>For a moment, I imagine winning the Cure for Cody. On one hand, after he’s better, I could be all quiet-hero and never mention how difficult the race was. People will talk behind my back and say, </i>She’s so brave. She never even brings it up, but we know how it must have been terrible. That Tella, she’s amazing.<i><br />On the other hand, I could go for martyr-who-will-never-let-it-go. I could shove it in Cody’s face every chance I got. I’d be like, </i>Hey, Cody, enjoying that doughnut? You wouldn’t be if I hadn’t saved your ass.”</blockquote><br />She’s a great narrator, and I felt fully involved in what was going on throughout the book. I felt like I was right in it with her, and this is also really cleverly done through the character dynamics. It all bring so much to the story – firstly through Tella’s love for her brother, then through her relationships with the others - particularly with Madox and Guy. Oh Guy *dreamy sigh*. I love the way the relationship between them develops from their very first meeting. He is dangerous and intriguing, and I really like how his character is slowly revealed along their journey. The encounters between them have that ‘zing’ that I crave between book characters, and I loved every little moment.<br /><br />This book is action-packed! There’s hardly a quiet moment, and when there is, it’s packed with humour, drama, and yes, even a bit of romance (woohoo!), and I was enthralled. We do get some questions answered, and I will admit I was a little squinty eyed during the explanations (really?), but there is still a lot to learn, so I withhold my final judgement until all is revealed. I’m really happy with the way the story progressed (the good and the bad), and while I wouldn’t call the ending a cliffhanger, the story is definitely left wide open, and I will be waiting with great anticipation for what is sure to be a thrilling conclusion. <br /><br />Bravo Victoria Scott for being brave enough to bring us such big story! I loved it – 4 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4895936562840284045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/573782416" />
    <a title="Stuti (Turmeric isn&#39;t your friend.   <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545537469" href="/book/show/16069167-fire-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship?shelf=crappy-creepy-romance">crappy-creepy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573782416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16215986818602204576"><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YMZsqDZM8Ic' rel='nofollow noopener'>Did you see the stylish kids in the riot<br/>Shovelled up like muck<br/>Set the night on fire<br/>Wombles bleed truncheons and shields?</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400134._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400135._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391499111ra/8400136.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Just refreshing thy memories.</i><br/><br/>Everyone wants to be them, for some reason. Everyone wants a Hunger Games, only without Panem, without Katniss, without Gale or Peeta or President Snow and the heartbreak and fire and tears and dead sisters and ornamented corpses. Everyone wants a Hunger Games in the hopes to manipulate emotions, not to make you feel; everyone wants a Hunger Games b</span>
  <span id="freeText16215986818602204576" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YMZsqDZM8Ic" rel="nofollow noopener">Did you see the stylish kids in the riot<br>Shovelled up like muck<br>Set the night on fire<br>Wombles bleed truncheons and shields?</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400134._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400135._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391499111ra/8400136.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Just refreshing thy memories.</i><br><br>Everyone wants to be them, for some reason. Everyone wants a Hunger Games, only without Panem, without Katniss, without Gale or Peeta or President Snow and the heartbreak and fire and tears and dead sisters and ornamented corpses. Everyone wants a Hunger Games in the hopes to manipulate emotions, not to make you feel; everyone wants a Hunger Games because that is the, like, THE most romantic setting for a budding love, amiright? Everyone wants to feel sorry for themselves, to save rapist psychopaths, to meet rapist psychopaths because the only villain we CAN have is either a long dead psychopath whose legacy continues till this moment(because the descendants are a horde of white, white sheep) or a rapist psychopath, which is all that he is. BECAUSE, a girl won't have survived through desert and sun and bugs, her survival won't matter if there's not a singular rapist psychopath to escape and kill.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400137._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fire &amp; Flood. Can't figure out the title, can't figure out the cover. I have some theories but I'm not interested in sharing them, chiefly because I'm not interested in this book, which is basically an assortment of HG arena's etc etc and <i>Michelle Rowan's Countdown</i>, another book I don't recommend. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825458283?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Litchick has done an effective job of equating the Hunger Games and Fire &amp; Flood.</a> Premise, momentary characters, the stone that sets in motion the ripples of the book, trains and pins and please do get the gist.<br><br>I have taken awhile to compile my thoughts about the book, but all I've been able to manage is basically:<br><br>What a rip-off!<br>What a cop-out!<br>What a stereotypically un-developed character!<br>What a lacking premise!<br>And once more, what a cop-out!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400138.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Except, I didn't really spend all that time thinking about the book; I had better things to do, like avoiding thinking about the book.<br><br>Here's Tella, a protagonist who's a little vain, a little whiny, laughing and criticizing her own self. In the middle of nowhere, her brother's dying and she pops in to check every moment that he's not dead, just asleep. I decide I'm going to like her.<br><br>Chapters later.<br><br>Here's Tella, having decided to enter a possibly hoax/dangerous competition to get the Cure that could save her brother, or so they day. We don't know who they are. She's crying and cutting her hair, having almost dropped out of the game because of her naive fascination and deliberation. Although the last part wanted to punch her into warp speed, I decide I'm going to like her.<br><br>Chapters later.<br><br>Here's Tella where coincidence happens, irks me a bit but I relinquish my personal peeves for once. She stalks the guy, I like. She might not have experience, but there could possibly be a head that works on her head. I decide I like her. <br><br>Soon after.<br><br>Here's Tella, meeting new people, hating a girl, Harper(whom I like still), because she can take charge and look beautiful; is gleeful because Harper has stretchmarks which could be an indicator that she was once fat in the past. I struggle to like her.<br><br>Interlude.<br><br>Why would you like if she were fat in the past, Tella? I want a reason. Is it because there are high school bulllies who find perverse satisfaction in playing on the insecurity of other people, fat people? Because these creatures bully other people, people who might be fat? Because by this reasoning, Harper might have once been bullied, and we should be gleeful about that? Or was it something completely different? Because if Harper was fat once, it means once upon a time, she wasn't as beautiful as she is now? Because somehow, people who are fat can't be beautiful? Or because beauty/thinness is a desirable character trait, and obesity is a sin, a mistake, an undesirable CHARACTER TRAIT?<br><br>Pissed me off, it did. BUT I decided to give her the benefit of doubt, decided she might improve later on, decided she was supposed to be an unlikable character and she'd progress. Unfortunately, since there comes along no other beautiful, thin person, we never will know, right?<br><br>Interlude over.<br> <br>Some time later.<br><br>Coincidences happen, AGAIN, I stop believing in the story. Out of hundreds upon hundreds of competitors, she stumbles upon the one handsome guy who's been rude to her and alternately helped her, once more. And he decides to join them.<br><br>They figure out where the next flag will be because it is all so simple. <br><br>Some time later.<br><br>Here's Tella, meeting the rapist psychopath. It goes on and he sexually harasses her but it's all fucking all right, amiright? It's still okay to let him continue with them; it's okay that he's 17-ish and deranged and rapist, and why haven't you fucking offed him yet, or maybe left him tied up somewhere in the middle of nowhere, where you fucking are? This is a race to death, not a fucking competition for deliverance from evils that tempt you!(And frankly evil wouldn't be tying up/incarcerating/castrating a guy like that, who is simply a psychopathic rapist and nothing else because whoever heard of villains with proper characterization?) <br><br>You are not here to emerge a newly fucking sanctified angel, you are here to emerge a victor with the cure that could save your brother!<br><br>And if you have a blue-eyed protector to save you every time, other girls this dude could prey on don't! You have a weapon, use it! Fucking idiot.<br><br>Here's where I lose lack of all chronologicality and order of events. Here's where I mark the beginning of a spoiler.<br><br>Here's why, I think, she didn't kill him earlier, with the support of her comrades and shit: so she could kill him at the end, on a cliff or some other dramatic stupidity, after she's hurt and what other fucking crap, to pwll at our heartswings; it doesn't. And I didn't like it that she took action only when her fucking said out loud in clear, hostile words that he's going to kill her, when she'd already felt his tongue in her mouth forcibly, so we could all see him in his perverted glory. <br><br>But... she kills him. I was glad.<br><br>SPOILER OVER<br><br>There are support genetically-engineered animals. They were cute, they hatched from eggs, but their inclusion was obviously a ploy to ensure Tella's longevity, which couldn't have been left to herself. The littlest problem they encounter, mmmmmmm, what to do, we can't do shit...mmmmm...oh look! one of our animals can help us with his/her magical abilities because he/she is tired of us mmmmmm-ing anf fake-ruminating on our asses and doing shit. &lt;--- This was the cop-out. This renders the survival part of this novel obsolete and redundant. Hunger Games? What a joke!<br><br>At first, I was angry that this book tried to be so much like the Hunger Games. Now, I'm just angry because it didn't even try to capture the essence of what made Hunger Games so miserable and hooking and heartbreaking; simply took the premise and over-simplified it. <br><br>They have genetically-engineered animal, yet the most adverse adversity they face is survival in the desert without supplies.<br><br>I've seen this in real life, on Discovery channel, without these animals to help. I remember now, these animals are called Pandoras!<br><br>The background story: it's stupid, it's given, it's fucking unbelievable. That about sums it up. Take my word for it.<br><br>THE BLUE-EYED GUY.<br>THE KNIGHT IN SHINING ARMOR.<br>THE OAFISH BEAST.<br>ALWAYS AND FOREVER READY TO SAVE HIS DISNEY PRINCESS.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400139._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Liam Neeson is awesome and Guy so isn't. This meme has no business here but I've always wanted to use this one.</i><br><br>AND DID I MENTION HOW USELESS TELLA IS WHEN IT COMES TO HERSELF? SE WAS AND SHE IS, AND BY this point, I'd already decided to not like her, and I'd already decided that I didn't like her. One or two times is okay, thrice I can grant but every fucking time? Challenges are meant to be overcome, not to be put aside for the knight in the fucking white armor. I hated the knight; Tella tried to give him, but he didn't have any personality. <br><br>Just a machine that has one code in its programming: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391512161i/8402824._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>DISCLAIMER: That was crap, I hope you don't expect it to work; I'm not good with this whole techy-programmy C++, even the children's handywork. <br><br>In the end, all boiled down to romance. Because that's what mattered.<br><br><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YMZsqDZM8Ic" rel="nofollow noopener">You know I cherish you my love.</a><br><br>Except it's less believable than the song. Because the song is awesome, the book isn't. <br><br>BUT HARPER WAS AWESOME! She survives, she has weaknesses, she has character, she breaks down, she likes, she has someone to save and she puts that before everything else. SHE MADE THIS BOOK A-OK.<br><br>Intial reaction:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391499111ra/8400140.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I've got my cool gathered and all:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400141.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>SO obviously the worst thing will happen to her. <br><br>I do NOT recommend this book. I recommend Oreos and Doge memes and Adventure Time and Katniss Everdeen and <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0460791/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fall</a> and other miscellaneous people and things and books, but not <i>Fire &amp; Flood</i>.<br><br>G'bye, now!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391499111i/8400142.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Review copy provided by publishers.</i></span>
